Having completed for you, children, this book, which is the final treatise on medicine with its completion, and having attained its end through its expositions and declarations, it seemed to me that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is a part of the practice of surgery, that is, of surgery with the hand.
Since the practice of surgery is neglected in our region and in our time, entirely private, until perhaps its knowledge perished and its trace was cut off, and nothing remained of it except small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which were altered by hands, and error and hesitation befell them, until its intentions were closed and its power was estranged; it seemed to me that I should revive it with the arrangement of this treatise, in it according to the way of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation; and that I would come with the forms of the instruments of cautery, and the other instruments of the craft, with the addition of the declaration, and with the hastening of what is necessary.
The reason why a skilled practitioner of surgery is not found with his hands in our time is that the art of medicine is long, and its author must be exercised beforehand in the knowledge of anatomy, as Galen narrated, until he knows the supports of the limbs, and their shapes, and their connections and separations, and has knowledge of the bones, nerves, tendons, and their numbers, and their exits, and the pulsating and still veins, and the places of their exits.
And therefore Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, but with a work is little, and especially in the art of the hand.
We, however, have already spoken of that in the introduction to this book.
Because whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have said concerning anatomy is not free from falling into error, whereby people are killed; as I have seen many of those who are formed in this knowledge, and boast of it without knowledge, and without experience.
This is because I saw a foolish physician cut a scrofulous abscess on a woman's neck, and cut some arteries in her neck; wherefore the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead in his hands.
And I saw another physician, who presumed to extract a stone from a man who had advanced in age, and the stone was large. Therefore, he reached it, and extracted it with a fragment of the bladder. Therefore, the man died on the third day.
And I myself had already been called to extract it; and I saw from the size of the stone, and the condition of the sick man, that he would die.
And I saw another physician, who was receiving a stipend from a certain Duke of our land for medicine; and it happened to a black eunuch, who was with him, a fracture in his leg near the heel: and the physician, in his ignorance, hurried and bound the fracture over the wound with cushions and splints with strong constriction, and did not allow the wound an outlet.
Then he discharged him according to his desires. Afterwards, he dismissed him after a few days, and commanded him not to loosen the bandage; and it stood thus until his leg and foot were suppurated, and he came to destruction.
I was therefore called to him; and I hurried to loosen the bandage; and tranquility followed, and he escaped from his pains.
However, the corruption had already become established in the limb; and I was unable to restrain it.
Therefore, the corruption ceased to travel in the limb, until it perished.
And I saw another physician, who pierced the cancerous abscess; and it ulcerated after days, until its malice was magnified with its owner.
That is because when the cancer is pure from melancholic humor, then it is not necessary to reach it with iron at all, unless it is in a limb that can tolerate having the whole of it cut off.
And therefore, my sons, it is necessary for you to know that surgery, with the hand, is divided into two divisions: namely, surgery to which health is associated; and surgery with which there is danger in many dispositions.
And I have already aroused in every place of this book, where surgery comes, in which there is terror and fear.
Therefore it is necessary for you to beware of that, and to cut it short, so that fools do not find a way to speak and to dishonour.
Therefore, receive the measure with care and protection, and your sick with ease and firmness, and use the better path leading by God's grace to health and praiseworthy succession; and abandon terrible illnesses difficult to heal; and remove your minds from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation may enter into your faith and your well-being.
For there remains more for your glory, and more sublime in this world, and ultimately more for your possessions.
For Galen has already said in some of his admonitions. Do not treat a bad illness, lest you be called a bad physician.
Now, however, I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
First chapter.
Concerning the cautery with fire, and the cautery with a sharp medicine, the subject matter, and the order, from head to foot, and the forms of instruments, and the tools of the cautery: and everything necessary in the operation.
Second chapter.
Concerning the incision and perforation, phlebotomy and cupping, and wounds: and the extraction of arrows, and similar things to those: and the whole subject matter, ordered by the forms of instruments.
Third chapter.
Concerning the restoration, and dislocation, and the cure of twisting, and similar things to those: the subject matter, ordered from head to foot, and the forms of instruments.
But before I recount the operation with it, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of its benefits and harms, and in what constitution it is to be applied.
I say, therefore, that the discussion of the quality of the cautery's benefit and harm is a lengthy and subtle discussion, a matter of knowledge and a hidden secret.
Many wise men have spoken on it, and disagreed on it; and for me, a little from their pronouncements suffices, fearing the extension.
I say, therefore, that the cautery is beneficial to every constitution, which is with matter and without matter: except for two constitutions, which are a hot constitution without matter, and a dry constitution without matter.
However, they disagreed in the hot and dry constitution with matter. For some said that the cautery is helpful in it. And others said the opposite, namely that the cautery is not suitable in a sickness which arises from heat and dryness; because the nature of fire is heat; and it is unsuitable that a sickness of heat and dryness be cured with heat and dryness.
And he who says the opposite of this said: that through the cautery is help given in every hot and dry illness which occurs in human bodies; because when you compare the human body and its humours to the constitution of fire, you find the human body cold.
And I myself say through his speech, because through experience it has already revealed that to me several times.
However, it is not fitting that one apply it [the cautery] unless one has already been proven and practiced in the final exercise of cautery, and knows the diversity of human constitutions, and the disposition of illnesses within themselves, and their causes, and their accidents, and the duration of those illnesses.
However, there is no fear from the other constitutions; and especially in cold and moist illnesses. For all physicians have already agreed on them [cold and moist illnesses]; and they have not disagreed on the help provided by the cautery in them.
And know, children, that from the secret of healing by cautery with fire, and its goodness over cautery with burning medicine, is that fire is simple, whose action does not reach except the limb that is cauterized, and does not harm another limb joined to it, except with a small harm.
However, the action of burning medicine reaches that which is distant from the limbs, and perhaps causes a difficult-to-heal illness in the limb, and perhaps kills it.
But fire, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do that unless it overflows.
Now indeed, that has become known to us through experience, because of the length of service and study with the art, and the standing on the truth of things; and because of that, I excuse myself from the length of discourse.
And if it were not so, because it is not permitted to this book of mine, I would reveal to you the hidden secret in fire, and the quality of its operation on the bodies of its expulsion, by which it expels illnesses, demonstrated by a philosophical, demonstrative discourse, which would be sharpened by your minds.
And know, children, that they disagree on the time in which the cautery should be applied, and place a better time in the spring.
And I say that cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harm that is incidental to the time is submerged in the benefit which is drawn along with the cautery. And especially if the cautery is for pains from necessary, strong, swift pains, which do not tolerate slowness; because it is feared from them that a greater harm may occur than the slight harm that enters because of the time.
And do not let it enter your minds, O children, that which only the common people and foolish physicians fear, namely that the ailment which is cured by cautery does not always return; and they consider this a consequence, and the matter is not as they think; because cautery is not, except in place of medicine, which alters the complexion and dries the humidities that are the cause why pains occur.
However, cautery surpasses medicine in the swiftness of its health, and the strength of its operation, and the vehemence of its dominion; and it is possible that the illness may return at some hour of time according to the complexion of the sick person, and the location of their illness, and its strength; and that which is prepared in their body from the aggregation of superfluities in it; and that which reaches them in their acquisition from foods, and similar things from such causes, unless it is the illness in which cautery is administered.
A subtle illness in a limb, of few superfluities and humidities, like the cautery of a tooth, on account of pain, and similar things to it, it is possible, indeed, that that pain will not return in it. But that happens in few.
But indeed the talk of the common people, that cautery is the last resort of medicine, is correct speech; not as they intend it, however, because they believe that there is no cure which compares with medicine, nor with anything after the cautery has passed.
However, the matter is the opposite of that, and the idea that cautery is the last resort of medicine is not so, unless when we administer modes of treatment for an illness, and those remedies do not work; then, at the end of the matter, we administer cautery, and it works; then, from this, it falls that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention that the common people and many foolish physicians understand.
However, the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron; and they did not say this except because of the equality of gold and the excellence of its substance; and they said that the place of the cautery does not produce pus. But that is not absolutely so; because I have already tested it, and found that it does not do so in some bodies without others.
And cautery with it is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you make a cautery of gold in fire, you are not shown when it is heated to the quantity you wish, because of the redness of the gold; and when it quickly approaches cold, and if you add more heat to it, it melts in the fire and turns into sheets.
Therefore, the craftsman falls from that into a dilemma: and because of that, cautery with iron is quicker and nearer for us in appropriateness for the operation.
And I have indeed already arranged this chapter on cautery, according to chapters; and I have arranged them from head to foot, so that those seeking what they want from it may be relieved.
Chapter II.
This cauterization benefits by mastering the humidity and coldness above the brain; these two are the causes of headaches, and the multitude of flowing humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and the multitude of sleep, and toothache, and throat pain: and universally all sickness that occurs from coldness, such as paralysis, and headaches, epilepsies, and apoplexies, and similar illnesses to them.
The method of cauterization is, that you instruct the sick person: that he be emptied first with a cleansing, dissolving medicine on the head for three nights, or four, according to what the strength of the sick person, and his age, and his custom requires.
Then instruct him to shave his head with a razor. Then make him sit between your hands square, so that he has already placed his hands on his chest.
Then place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever, therefore, your middle finger arrives, mark that place with cautery.
Then apply the olive-shaped cautery iron: this is its form.
Then place it on the marked place with cautery, with a descent, so that your hand is gradually tightened, and you will turn it. Then quickly lift your hand and look at the place.
If you see a quantity of alkiel or zeuherbi already exposed from the bone, then lift your hand. And if not, repeat the application of your hand with the iron itself, or with another if it has cooled: until the bones I spoke of appear.
Then take some salt, and dissolve it in water, and soak the cloth in it, and place it on the place, and leave it for three days.
Then place the cloth soaked in butter on it, and leave it on the place until the scab of the fire is destroyed. Then treat it with the four-drug ointment, until it is healed.
Now they say that the more a wound remains open, the more it discharges pus: wherefore it is better and more helpful.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized down to the bone, and the cautery should be held until a certain thickness of bone is burned.
Then that which is burned from the bone should be scraped off, then treated.
And others say that it is necessary to proceed with the cautery to the extreme, until it makes an impression in the bone, so that the bone falls, which happens as if a kirate form were there: or like the instrument which women place on an infused alphabet small: and they believe that vapors of the head are exhaled from this place, and the wound should be left open for a long time.
Then it should be treated until it consolidates.
However, these two kinds of cautery do not seem to me to be useful except in some people, according to a fearful way.
And to leave it, in my opinion, is better with the preservation of his health.
For the head is weakened by the disruption of its natural continuity, as we have observed in other limbs; and especially when the head of the sick person is naturally weak. And indeed, the first kind of cautery is safer and better in my opinion, and I use it: therefore, operate with it to ensure health.
Chapter III.
When chronic pain occurs throughout the head, and it lingers in the sick person, and they use leeches, and cupping, and head-purgations, and oils, and poultices. And especially if it has already been cauterized with the one cautery, which we have described, and none of those things benefit it: then consider. For if the head of the sick person is of strong natural constitution, and is not weak, and encounters intense cold, then cauterize with another cautery beneath it a little. Then cauterize it itself on every horn of its head with a cautery, so that it does not pierce the skin, and a quantity of bone, as we described, is not exposed. And cauterize it with one cautery in the back of its head, in the place called the *vas* (vessel), which is the place where a cupping glass is placed; and raise your cautery in this area, and do not expose bone. For the sick person experiences intense pain on account of it, and different from the pain of the other cauteries of all the head.
And I shall say this cautery is in its proper place; and it should be a cautery with which the horns of the head are cauterized, and its back [occiput] with a finer cautery, with which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Chapter Four.
When pain and throbbing occur in a part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and the head is purged with cleansing medicines, and the remaining treatment, which I have described in the divisions of diseases, is administered, and yet that does not wholly benefit it: then cauterization in it is according to two methods: either cauterization with a burning sharp medicine, or with iron.
The cautery with a burning sharp medicine is: to take one clove of garlic, and peel it, and cut off its extremities from both sides. Then open the place of pain with a broad lancet, until a space is made under the skin, in which the clove is inserted.
Then insert it into the space under the skin, until it is hidden; then bind it over with a suitable constriction with a bandage, and leave it for fifteen hours; then loosen it and remove the garlic, and leave the wound for two or three days; afterward apply a poultice soaked in butter, until the place produces pus; then treat it with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish to do it with certain burning medicines, which I have written in the twelfth treatise, on Burning Medicines.
The cauterization of it with iron, is according to this method. A cautery of fire, whose form is this.
And it is called a Clavil, because the shape of its head is like the shape of a nail, in which there is a certain curve, and in its middle is a small eminence.
Then place it on the spot, and hold your hand; and you turn the iron slowly with speed; and let the amount that is burned be from the thickness of the skin, like half of it. And raise your hand, so that the artery, which is below, is not burned, and a flow of blood occurs.
Then soak a poultice in salt water, and place it on the spot, and leave it for three days; then place the poultice with butter; afterward treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicrania with the second cautery's knife-point. And beware of the incision of the artery in this hemicrania, not properly an old one.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in an old hemicrania.
When you treat hemicrania, along with what we said in the previous treatment, and what we said in the divisions of illnesses, and if treatment does not help; and you see from the illness that what we said about the first cautery with medicine, or with cautery with fire, does not suffice, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery knife until it whitens, after marking the site of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger, or thereabouts; and place your hand on one side, and press it until you cut the artery and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to beware of the continuation of the jaw, which moves during chewing, lest the side or the nerve that moves it be burned, whence spasm may result.
And be on guard, and cautious about the flow of blood from the artery that has been cut. For in its cutting lies danger, and especially for him who does not know what he is doing, and is not studious nor experienced: and he abandons the operation with that in the first place.
And I will come with a reminder of the regimen for blood flow arising from the artery according to its manner, and in its place in this book.
If, however, you see from the illness that this cautery is not sufficient for him, and you see the body of the sick person tolerating the cautery in the middle of the head, as we have narrated, treat the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cautery that we spoke of in the chapter on the extraction of the artery with the cautery having two knives. For cauterization is better than this and more beneficial.
Concerning the method of cauterization for ear pain.
When pain in the ear occurs from cold, and is treated with remedies, and with the other treatment that we have discussed in the division, and the pain is not removed, then apply a cautery with fire: and that is what is called a Point, whose shape is this.
Then apply the points, after its ignition, in a circuit around the entire ear, as it revolves; or in a circuit around each ear, if pain is present in both simultaneously. And withdraw the cautery slightly from the root of the ear, after you have marked the places with ink; and the cautery's quantity should be ten points in each ear, and approximately of that size.
Then treat the places until they are healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in a case of torture.
Chapter VII.
Torture which is treated with cauterization is only of the types that occur from phlegm, according to what we said in the divisions of illnesses.
And avoid cauterization of the type that occurs from desiccation and nerve spasm.
When you treat this type of torture with leeches, and head purges, and gargles, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize the afflicted with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and a second a little lower from its temporal location, and a third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery opposite the affected part. Because softening does not occur, unless in the part that appears healthy.
And the form of the cauterization is that you cauterize it with the cautery directly on the upper extremity of the ear under the horn of the head a little: and another in the temporal region: whose length is according to the length of the thumb. And place your hand with the cautery until a quantity equal to half the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a type from a knife, whose form has been previously stated: however, it is not a little more delicate than that, as you see: and it is necessary that the knife in it have a little superfluous thickness.
Then treat the places, with what has preceded, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in ancient apoplexy.
When apoplexy is prolonged, and you have treated it with what we have said, and your treatment is not effective, and the patient does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on each horn of his head, and with a cautery in the middle of the head, as we said, and with a cautery on the back of the head, according to what has gone before: and the method of the cautery be according to what has gone before.
Also, he is cauterized with a cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and this is the most extreme.
Then he is treated with what has gone before.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in the drink be given first to the sick large hyerae, and pills that cleanse the brain.
Then shave the entire head of the sick person, and place on the back of his head a plaster of mustard described in the treatise on plasters: and place it repeatedly.
For that is the method of cautery, and do it according to the same order which I said there.
If therefore he is cured by it, it is good. If not, then make three cauteries on the back part of his head, which shall be descending from the upper part of the head down to the lower part of the eye: and place between each cautery the thickness of a finger.
Then treat the cautery with what preceded it.
If however you wish an addition, and the sick person is able to tolerate it, then make a cautery in the middle. If you wish an addition, then cauterize him above the two horns.
Then treat him until he is healed, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the form that was given before.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in paralysis and softening.
Chapter X.
You should proceed in cleansing the head with hyeeris, and with what we have said.
Then shave the patient's head; afterward, cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery on each horn of the head, and with a cautery on its back, and with three on the vertebrae of the neck.
However, if the illness requires softening of the body with more than those [mentioned], and the patient is a weak tolerator, and the illness is severe, then cauterize him with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and the last with a cautery, until a large portion of his skin is burned, and raise your hand. Then treat him until he is healed; and thus the cautery of Oliuare.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized, unless that whose epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary that you first cleanse his brain with leeches, and with the rest of the treatment that we have described in the division; when the sick person is strong, or is tolerant of taking medicine.
However, if it is a child who does not tolerate medicine, then a gargle and chewing to cleanse the brain are administered, for many days beforehand, along with improved food.
Then shave his head, afterwards cauterize him with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what has gone before in the method; and with another cautery on his occiput, and with a cautery on every horn of his head. If, however, the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize him with the cauteries I described for paralysis, and for the softening of the body over the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back; and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the method which preceded.
If, however, the patient is a child, then apply a thin cautery, according to this method.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries that we have described for paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess of the downward tendency towards melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give him a drink that will cleanse his brain, according to what was previously stated in the division; then shave the patient's head, and afterward make a neatly fashioned pad of linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head, and the patient, seated upright, must be held securely on all sides.
Then apply the liniment. And it is best made from old sheep's butter. And heat it over a fire with a moderate heat, which the finger can tolerate when it is inserted into it. Then apply it to the middle of his head in a circle, and leave it until it cools.
Do this to the sick person once a week, with the rest of his good regime, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small punctures throughout it, provided that you hold the cautery iron: indeed, let it smell.
For this kind of cautery moistens the brain with quality.
Then place over it a cloth soaked in butter, or chicken fat.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in descending water to the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When the beginning of water in the eye is declared to you by the signs that I said in the division, then begin and drink the weak one, with that which cleanses his head.
And keep him from all moisture, and have him sit in a bath, fasting for a few days.
Then command him to shave his head, and cauterize him in the middle of his head. Then cauterize him above the two temples with two cauteries, if it is the beginning of the descent of water into both eyes at once; or from one side, if the beginning of water is in one eye: and cut away with the cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let the cauteries be in length equal to the width of the temples; and beware of a flow of blood.
If you see anything from him, then cut it away immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I will come with the knowledge that is in the extraction of arteries, and the cutting of them, and the caution from the flow of blood.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck, under the two bones, with two cauteries finally applied.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in ancient weeping.
When the tears of the eyes are ancient, persistent, and situated over the veins and arteries that are visible on the outer head, confirming that it arises from cold, phlegmatic superfluities, then cauterize with the same cautery as I described at the beginning for descending water, a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries above the two temples, and two cauteries on the neck under the two bones. And if it requires further treatment, then cauterize it on every side of the eye's cavity, above the edge of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a nasal odor.
When you treat it, as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then act quickly and give the weak person infirmed cochias for three nights; then shave his head and cauterize it with a middle cautery, together with an olive-shaped cautery. Then cauterize it with a key-shaped cautery, with two cauteries, above the two eyebrows, beneath the hair a little.
And guard against the artery, lest you strike it.
And this is the form of the key-shaped cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in the softening of the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, with this crescent-shaped cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows slightly with two cauteries on every side; and let them be distant from the two temples; and let the length of each cautery be according to the length of the eyebrow; and do not move your hand with the cautery to the end, but according to the amount that the third eyelid is burned.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the eyelid when the hairs are inverted, piercing the eye.
The cautery in it is according to two methods: either a cautery with fire, or a cautery with a burning medicine.
In cautery with fire, beforehand, tell the sick person to remove his hairs, if he is one of those who cleanses them, until they are extended and made equal. If, however, they pierce him near their origin, then bind his eyes with a strip so that they do not move until they grow.
When therefore they grow and are equal, then place the head of the sick person in your lap; then mark above the eyelids of his eyes with ink, a sign that is according to the shape of a myrtle leaf; and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs.
Then place a cotton swab soaked in egg white, or in psyllium mucilage, on the eye.
Then apply the cautery, whose form is this.
Then cauterize over the figure which you marked gradually in many stages, until the surface of the skin, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, is entirely burned away.
And the sign of the success of your work is: that if you see the eyelid already contracting, and the hairs rising near the puncture of the eye.
Therefore raise your hand then, and leave it for three days.
Then place on it a poultice with butter, until the eschar is removed. Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
If any of the hairs return after an hour, and the eyelid softens, then again cauterize that place, as you did at first.
If however the hairs are in the lower eyelid, then cauterize it until it is raised to its natural position and the hairs are even so that they do not prick the eye.
You should instruct the sick person to let the hairs fall out until they are lengthened and even. Make a shape of a myrtle leaf from paper or cloth.
Then take from known soap, and from unsoaked lime, one ounce or nearly that of each: then grind them together with good rubbing, and do it quickly so that it does not grow cold. Then spread a piece of that (mixture) onto the paper you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it over the eyelid of one or two eyes. And place under the eye a cloth soaked in egg white: and let the sick person's head be in your bosom.
And place your index finger on the medicine, and press it for a little while. And you should move it whenever the sick person feels the medicine's biting: because its biting is found to be like fire.
So long as he finds this biting, then remove the medicine and move it with your finger. When the biting ceases, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And then consider, if you see the eyelid rising, as it rises with contraction with fire, or with incision, it is well; and if not, then again place medicine on the place where the medicine does not imprint, and does not darken, until your operation is equal, and the eye contracts.
Then place on it a poultice with butter, until the skin of the burn is eradicated. Then treat it with diaphanicon ointment, or another, until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you at the operation, that you guard the last guard, lest something of the medicine fall into the eye.
If the eyelid softens after days, and something struggles from the hairs into the eye, then again place medicine on that place which softens from the eyelid properly, as you did at first. Then treat it until it is healed.
And this is the form of the myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men are diversified in size and smallness. Therefore, according to that, let your consideration be; and the way of rectitude is not hidden from him who has a study of this art.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a tear duct fistula.
When you treat a fistula, as with what we have said in the divisions of illnesses, and your treatment does not benefit: then, it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method.
Tell the sick person to place their head in your lap, and let the attendant hold their head in their hands in such a way that it does not move or shake with their head.
Then place a cautery, dipped in the white of an egg or in psyllium mucilage, over their eye. Then apply the cautery, whose shape is this.
Let it be concave, like the shape of a vulture's wing feather from one end, with which the cautery is made. And if you want it to be penetrating all the way to the other end, and if you want it held in this upward position.
However, this concave shape is better for your work.
Then express the fistula, if it is open, and extract the pus from it, and dry it; and if it is not open, then open it and extract its pus.
Then place the cautery, which is made very hot, upon it.
And hold your hand with the cautery near the eye, toward the part of the nose, so that your hand does not wander or the sick person is not disturbed; and place the cautery on the fat of the eye and corrupt it.
If therefore you reach the beginning of your cautery up to the bone, it will be well. And if not, then repeat the cautery once or twice, if you need it; and leave it for three days.
Then place a cloth with butter, and treat it with a drying ointment, until it is healed.
If forty days have passed and it is not healed, then place upon it a sharp corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and scrape it according to what comes in its chapter.
And there is another method of cautery of fistulas, which some of the first ones said. Direct your attention to the location of the fistula, and cut it open; then place within the fissure a fine camahan, that is, a fine cannula, whose form is this. And pour into it a quantity of a drachm of melted lead, and hold your hand with a good retaining cannula, and let the sick person not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run or reach his eye.
And it is necessary that you place upon the eye of the sick person a poultice soaked in egg white, or in water.
For lead burns the place of the fistula, and heals it with a marvelous cure.
If the fistula is healed with what we have said from cautery and treatment, that is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer a nasal opening, and to redirect the fistula to the course of the nose, according to where it will return to its own proper place.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in lip fissures.
Often fissures occur in the lip, which are called hairs, and especially on the lips of children.
Therefore, when you treat these fissures, as we said in the division of diseases, and the treatment does not help, then use a small knife cautery with fire, according to this form.
And its concavity should be according to the sharpness of the knife.
Then place it [the cautery] ignited quickly onto the fissures themselves, until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with a cautery, until it heals.
Concerning the method of cauterization in the fistula of the mouth.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth; then it produces pus, and breaks open; afterwards it becomes chronic, and runs pus, and a fistula forms; then you treat it, and treatment does not help it, then it is necessary to cauterize the fistula with a cautery according to its size. Then insert the hot iron into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches its depth and end; do it once or twice.
Then treat it afterward, with what we have said about treatment until it is healed.
If therefore the pus is removed and it heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place, and remove the corrupted bone according to what comes in its head.
Concerning the method of cauterization in softened gums and teeth.
When the gum softens due to moistures, and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines, and it does not help: then place the head of the sick person in your bosom.
Then with fire, a cautery, whose form will follow after this, so that you place the Cannula upon the tooth: and quickly insert into it the burning Cautery: and hold your hand for a short time, until the sick person feels the heat of the fire now having reached the root of the tooth.
And raise your hand: then repeat the Cautery several times, as you wish.
Then let the sick person fill their mouth with salt water, and hold it for one hour: and let them spit it out.
For the tooth that moves is strengthened, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupted moisture is dried.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in toothache.
When toothache is due to cold, or there is cold or a worm within it, and treatment with medicines does not help: then the cautery is applied to it in two ways: either cautery with butter, or cautery with fire.
The cautery with butter is to take cow's butter, and boil it in an iron spoon, or in a vessel. Then take a piece of cotton, and wrap it around the end of the probe. Then immerse it in the boiled butter; and quickly place it on the aching tooth, and hold it until it cools; then repeat this several times, until the power of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, immerse wool or cotton in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth; and place a heated iron upon it, until the fire reaches the depth of the tooth's cavity.
Its cauterization with fire is to apply a bronze tube or an iron tube. And let there be something of thickness in his body, so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the sick man's bone.
Then take the cautery, whose form will come; and place it on that tooth; and hold your hand, until the cautery cools.
Do it several times, for the pain will be removed, either on that same day or on another day.
And it is necessary, during the application of that cautery, that the sick man fill his mouth with good butter and hold it for one hour; then he should spit it out.
And this is the form of the cautery.
Cauterize with whichever extremity of force is possible; and this is the form of the cannula.
Concerning the method of cauterization in strophules.
When strophules are caused by phlegm and cold humors, and are not yielding to digestion by medicines, and force is needed to speed their digestion, then use a concave cautery, whose shape is this.
Having two open ends, so that smoke may escape from the cautery at the other end; and place it, heated, upon the abscess once, and twice, if it needs it, until it reaches the depth of the abscess.
If the abscess is small, then place the cautery according to the size of the abscess.
Then leave it for three days, and place on it a poultice infused in butter, until that which the fire has burned away is removed.
Then treat it with a tooth ointment, until the shape of the cannula is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in hoarseness of voice and constriction of breathing.
When humidities overcome the bronchial passage, and especially when it is with a cold temperament, then it is necessary that the sick person be evacuated in the first place with dissolving medicines.
Then cauterize it in the nocrati at the root of the throat in the depressed place: and be careful not to reach the throat with the cautery, nor the skin, except a certain part of it.
Then cauterize it with another cautery at the joint of the neck at the last vertebra thereof, and let the cautery be a small one according to the method which preceded.
Then treat it with what preceded, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in diseases of the lungs and cough.
When cough and lung disease are from cold humors, and the patient does not have fever, nor consumption, and the illness is old, then cauterize him with two cauteries above the fork in low, smooth, empty places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two nipples: and let the cautery be of a cannula according to the form that preceded.
And if you wish your cauterization to be by puncturing with a cautery, called a Point, whose form preceded in the puncturing of ear pain: and let the points be from thirty points up to, as it were, others.
Then treat him with that which preceded, until he is healed.
And now let the cautery have three branches: according to this form. Therefore, the cauterization is alleviated when you do it with three cauteries at once.
Chapter XXVII.
When the head of the arm is dislocated due to moisture, and does not return to its position after dislocation, until it is accustomed to returning, then it dislocates from a small movement that occurs as we have already testified, then you must first reduce the dislocation. Then the patient shall be laid on their back, or on their healthy side. Then lift the skin that is in the inner titillum towards the top with the fingers of your left hand: and if the joint is dislocated inwards.
Then having a cautery with two prongs of fire. Whose form is this.
Then cauterize the skin, until it penetrates it to the other side, and the figure of the cauterization will come with four cauteries.
And sometimes a cauterization is made with a cautery having three prongs, wherefore the figure of the cauterization is then of six cauteries: and the prongs are according to the fineness of the thread.
And this is the form of the cautery having three prongs.
And sometimes one is added to this manner, wherefore there are eight cauteries.
Then place on the cautery pounded leeks with salt. Then cause the infirm person to adhere to stillness, so that the limb does not move at any time, until it is strengthened.
And if the dislocation is upward, and rarely does it occur thus, then cauterize it above the shoulder with a clavicle cautery, or with many cauteries by pricking.
For the joint is strengthened, and moisture is removed: and the sick person is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When there are cold and numerous moistures in the stomach, until they draw it away from its disposition, and phlegms multiply within it, and constant methods of treatment do not help, then it is necessary that the sick person be laid on their back, and extend their legs, and their hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries, one cautery beneath the breast, the size of one finger's breadth with a cautery blade, and two cauteries below, on either side of the first cautery, until the shape of the cauteries forms a triangle. And elongate them [the cauteries] between each other so they do not join, when they will produce pus.
And the depth of the cautery should be the thickness of two-thirds of the skin.
And let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form, without addition; and if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach, according to this form, let the cautery by which this is done be one according to the form of a circle, according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by pricking it for him who is terrified by this cautery; and it is as if one marks a point on the stomach according to the size that one desires with ink; then cauterize it with a cautery of the point; then treat it with the treatment that preceded until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing a cold liver.
When pain in the liver occurs from cold and moisture, or from thick wind, until it departs from its natural complexion by the departure of superfluous matter, and the patient is treated with what we have said, and it does not help him: then it is necessary that the patient be laid on his neck, and that three cauteries be marked with ink according to this figure, and the same size on the liver below the hypochondria, where the human elbow reaches; and let the space between each cautery be according to the thickness of a finger; and let the cautery be straight according to the length of the body; and do not press your hand with the cautery too much.
And let the quantity of what is burned be, from the thickness of the skin, the quantity of half of it not added; and let the patient be standing on his feet.
If however he is not standing, then let him lie down, having now extended his legs and raised his arms.
This is the form of the cautery.
And it is possible for you, to cauterize these cauteries with a knife cautery, when you have subtlety and prudence in the art.
And guard yourself, lest you proceed too far in the cauterization, and the thickness of the entire skin is burned, wherefore the entire body is burned, and it reaches the intestines; because the skin there is delicate, know this therefore.
Concerning the method of cauterizing liver abscesses.
When discharge occurs, and you wish to know if the abscess is in the flesh of the liver, or in its tunic: then if it is in the flesh of the liver, it afflicts the sick person with pain and heaviness without sharpness; and if it is in the tunic of the liver, with the pain is a sharp vehemence: and you see now that the treatment has fatigued its physicians.
Therefore, the sick person must lie on their back on a pillow. Then mark the location of the abscess with a marking ink; then apply a cautery heated like a ray. And this is its form. And cauterize with it one cautery, until the entire skin is burned and reaches the pus, until all the pus comes out; then treat it with the treatment for discharges until it is healed.
And one should not use this type of cautery unless the one who studies the art of medicine has practiced it, and through whose hands such illnesses have come with experience several times: for only then should he dare to undertake such an operation.
But truly, to leave it alone is better for me.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Pleuresy.
The ancients said that a cautery with aristolochia roots should be used for a cold pleurisy in this manner. And it is, that you should receive from the dry long roots of aristolochia, one root longer than the others, which is found in it, and let it be as thick as a finger. Then immerse it in oil, and light it in fire. Then cauterize with one cautery at the point where the fork joins the neck, and with two small cauteries slightly sloping down on the part beneath the chin.
And with two cauteries also on that which is between the fifth and sixth ribs, sloping slightly backward; and with another cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from the back: one on that which is between the two shoulder blades; and with two cauteries from the two sides of the chest, lower than the cautery which is between the two shoulder blades.
And you should not compress your hand with the cautery, rather it should be in plain view, smelling the skin.
And some ancients have said that there are men who use a cautery of iron like a rod; and they ignite it, and insert it into that which is between the ribs, until it reaches the abscess itself, and pus comes out; as we said regarding liver abscess.
But in this perforation with the cautery there is fear that either the weak person dies immediately, or a fistula occurs in the place, which has no cure.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the spleen, Chapter XXXII.
When you treat the illness of the spleen, with what we said about treatment in the division of illnesses, and your treatment is of no use, then the cautery is on it according to three methods, which are all correct.
One of which is to make three cauteries, or four, by drawing a line along the length of the spleen, according to the figure of the liver cauteries, whose figure preceded.
And let there be between each cautery a quantity equal to the thickness of a finger, or more or less.
And let the method of the cautery be, as we said, in the cautery of the liver, equally.
And do not press your hand with the cautery; and let the infirm person lie supine on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: that you heat the cautery having two prongs, which we said in the chapter on the dislocation of the humerus; and raise the skin, which is directly over the spleen, where the left elbow of the infirm person reaches; and let your elevation of the skin be according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall along the length of the body.
Then insert the two very hot prongs until you penetrate the skin on the other side with them; then withdraw the cautery; therefore four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with another cautery having three prongs.
Then treat the cautery after you let it discharge pus for many days; for it is more beneficial than all the preceding treatments.
Concerning the method of cauterization in dropsy.
The cautery does not fall upon dropsy unless properly applied.
When you treat a dropsical patient with the methods of treatment, which we have described in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, then you should cauterize him with four cauteries around the navel, and one cautery on the stomach, and another cautery on the liver, and one cautery on the spleen, and two cauteries on the back between the vertebrae, and one directly on the chest, and another directly on the stomach; and let the depth of the cautery be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the cautery open, so that it emits pus for a long time.
And do not remove the sick person from treatment after the cautery with it; for it is necessary that two intentions gather for him: and healing will hasten to him with God's help.
The form of the cautery with which the abdomen is cauterized should be nail-shaped, according to its previous form; and the one with which the back is cauterized should be olive-shaped, according to its previous form.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the Feet and Legs.
When abscesses occur in a dropsy patient, and are filled with yellow water, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot in the area between the auricular and annular [bones]; and raise your hand with the cautery, and do not turn it; then raise your hand; and do not repeat it at all.
For the yellow water will sweat out, and the cautery should be of this form.
Then make two cauteries on each leg, and let the cautery be made with the blade-end of the cautery; and let the cautery be made along the length of the leg, one below the knee, and the other below that, approximately in the middle of the leg; and make two cauteries on each thigh; and leave the cautery open without treatment for a long time, so that some water sweats out from it; then treat it with the rest of what we have said.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in abdominal disorders.
Chapter XXXV.
When there is an abdominal disorder caused by cold and dampness, until it weakens the retentive and digestive powers in the stomach and intestines; and it is treated with methods of cure, and is not healed; and you see the sick person tolerating a cautery of great power, then cauterize him with a large cautery on his stomach, according to what has preceded in cauterizing the stomach with a circular cautery, and with four subtle cauteries around the navel, with a subtle clavus cautery; and with a large cautery on the alcatin above the alhosos, or with two cauteries.
And if you see excessive moisture, and the sick person tolerates it, then cauterize him with a cautery on the breastbone, and with a cautery on each hip; and perhaps add two small cauteries near the large one on the stomach.
For it is a beneficial treatment, whose help does not err.
Concerning the method of cauterizing Hemorrhoids.
Chapter XXXVI.
When in the anus are many old hemorrhoids, or one, and they are from thick, cold humors, or corrupted moisture, and are treated with what we said in the division, and the treatment does not help: then cauterize with three cauteries on the lower spine of the back, slightly triangularly under the almeidati, and with a cautery under the navel, as if with two fingers.
And if you think that his stomach is chilled, and his food is not digested, and you see his face becoming abscessed, then cauterize him on the stomach with a large cautery, according to what went before; and with a cautery on his liver, and another on his spleen, with a cautery iron; and leave the cautery open for some time; then treat him until he is healed.
Chapter XXXVII.
When you excise althelul, then heat the cautery that is like a ray. Then introduce the heated cautery into the excised althelul: and with the end of your hand, until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which the blood flows: do it once, or twice.
If therefore the althelul are many, then cauterize each one with the cautery according to what we have recounted. Then treat them with that which benefits them from ointments, until they are healed.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery on the alcatin, it is more effective in helping.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Chapter XXXVIII.
When the patient does not obey the incision and operation that we have described in its place, and is frightened by it, perhaps he is healed with a cautery.
When therefore a fistula occurs in someone, and becomes chronic, pus runs from it, and corrupt humors. Therefore it is fitting that you probe it with a fine probe. Then ascertain the depth of it with the probe.
Then heat the cautery, which is similar to a ray. Then introduce the heated cautery into the fistula itself and the amount in which the cautery entered.
And repeatedly apply the cautery to it, until all those corrupted bodies are burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to your need.
And beware of burning the nerve, if there is one there, or a major vein; or if the fistula goes to the bladder, or the body of the intestine, then beware of all these places.
And do not do this unless the fistula is in a fleshy place, and you judge that it is not penetrating.
Then treat the place until it is healed.
If, however, the place is sealed, and the matter is cut away from it, and remains like this for a long time, then you should know that it is now completely healed.
And if matter is not cut away from it, then you should know that it is penetrating, or a corrupt bone is within it, or something like that from those [sources], whose mention will come in its place.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the Kidneys.
When pain occurs in the kidneys from cold or from a large wind, and it is lessened because of that infirmity, then it is necessary to cauterize it on the almethen, over the kidneys themselves, cauterizing over each kidney with a clauili cautery, the mention of which preceded.
And perhaps we cauterize it a second time on the same almeidan. Therefore three lines will come. Therefore the last will be more helpful.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When weakness and softening of the bladder occur due to cold and dampness, so that the afflicted person cannot retain urine, then cauterize it on the lower part of the summit above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic comb begin. Cauterize with one cautery from the right side of the summit, and another from its left.  Let the length of each cauterization along the side be equal to the size of a thumb's node; and cauterize with a cautery of the lower back, or with two cauteries if that one is insufficient. Let this be in accordance with the preceding cautery's closure.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the womb.
When cold and dampness affect the womb, preventing conception, corrupting her menses, delaying their expulsion, and causing pain upon their arrival, then three cauteries should be applied around the navel, as was described in the cauterization of the bladder, and one cautery above the lower back, or two cauteries.  And let this cautery be the closing cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the anus in dislocation.
When mucous humors discharge into the anus, causing it to depart from its place, and the sign of this is that one leg is prolonged over the other when they are compared together, and the place of the dislocation is found empty in it.
Therefore, it is necessary to cauterize the affected area over the anus itself with a similar circular cautery, after you mark it with ink around its perimeter as it revolves, so that the anus falls in the middle of the circle.
If this cautery is not available to you, then cauterize it with three cauteries, with a large olive cautery, and let the depth of the cauterization be according to the thickness of the skin.
Then treat it until it heals.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Sciatica.
When pain occurs in the hip joint, and its cause is cold and dampness, and the patient is treated with what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and it becomes chronic, then it is necessary to relieve the patient of the gross humors with foul pills, or with artificial pills, and similar ones. Then cauterize it.
And the method of cautery in it is according to two methods: either cautery with burning medicines, or cautery with fire.
Cautery with fire is according to many methods.
One of which is to cauterize over the hip joint itself with three triangular cauteries, according to this form. And make them a good or bad depth. And let the space that is between each cautery be of the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
Sometimes however, cautery is made in the middle over the head of the hip itself. Therefore there are four cauteries.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose form preceded in the cauterization of the dislocation of the hip, one: so that there may be a circle containing the entire hip.
And burn the thickness of the entire skin.
This is the method of cautery in Sciatica, when the pain is adhering to the hip itself, and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
If however it extends to the thigh and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries on the thigh, over the place to which the infirm person there points, where the pain is, and with your cautery on the shin four fingers to the wild part for a short time: and let the cautery be a knife-like one.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the depth of the thickness of the skin.
If the infirm person indicates that the pain extends nearly to the toes of the foot, then cauterize it there where he indicates with a prick cautery, three, or four, or more, if it requires that.
And if he indicates the pain to be below the knee toward the leg, then cauterize it there with one knife-like cautery.
And beware in all your cauterizations, that you not proceed with the cautery to the point of burning the nerve, or a large artery, and thereby inflicting upon the infirm a bad harm or contraction.
And indeed I have already seen one and another, of those who cauterized above the ankle, and went too far in the cauterization, and the leg swelled up, until the swelling reached the foot, and the whole was perforated, and the whole foot was corrupted: then the belly dissolved, and death followed after that.
If the pain is in two parts simultaneously, cauterize each according to this method.
And some wise men said on the cauterization of the buttock, of which this is the method of cautery. Make a similar cautery of iron, whose diameter is half a palm: and let it be at its opening according to the thickness of a date seed, or a little less: and within that cautery let there be a third cautery.
And let the space that is between every cautery be by the amount of a thumb's knot: and let the cauteries be open on both sides: and let their height be like a knot, or two knots: and make for them a handle of iron fitting well into the cauteries.
Then let it be heated in fire until it glows red and throws off sparks: then let it be placed upon the box of the buttock of the sick man reclining on his healthy side. Therefore cauterize him with three round cauteries at one time.
Then leave him for three days. Afterwards apply plasters with butter, and leave the wound open for many days. Then treat him with ointment until he is healed.
Albucasis says, with this kind of cautery, O sons, we have used it little, because of the terror of its appearance, and because we have found few who can endure it.
However, it is a good cautery for one who endures it, and who finds its place with it.
A cautery, however, is with burning medicines, so that you make two samia having a perforated armilla, into which the hinge of its door descends, of bronze or iron, the length of a wall, whose height they shall have two knots, or like them.
And let the space between each be the thickness of a finger, and let them be open below and above, and let that which contains them be joined together, in this manner.
Then place it upon a box of ashes, the sick man lying on his healthy side. And press your hand upon the box of ashes firmly. Then pour between the two circles hot water, which has been heated with fire for a short time, and hold it for the amount of an hour's time.  And let the sick man endure its stinging and its burning, for he finds the stinging like fire, until the stinging subsides.
Then raise your hand with the instrument, and wash away the hot water from the entire ash with sweet water; then leave it for three days.
And place butter upon it, until the blackness of the burning is removed; and leave it for a number of days, and pus will run from it. For it is the ultimate in aid.
Then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
If the pain extends to the hip, or leg: make a poultice on it that contains water, as you did on the ash equally.
And this is the method of hot water; and I have already written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Take alkali and quicklime, both of one part: grind both, and place them in a new pot, whose lower part is perforated with one small hole, according to the quantity that the radius will enter: and place another glazed pot under the bottom of the pot: and pour over the alkali and lime from sweet water, which submerges both by a finger: after which you compress them with your hand with a good compression: and leave the pot until the sharp water descends into the lower part of the glazed pot.
Then collect all that water, and pour it over other lime; and strain, until it is renewed.
For it will then be very strong and sharp, which is administered in many surgical operations and in the cauterization of other limbs. Because it produces the operation of fire itself.
And from medicines, with which the anchas are cauterized, also such as tessie, and honey of anacardi, and lime with soap, so that both are mixed together.
And Galen, indeed, narrating, recounted the cure of a certain man from ancient times, by which the pain of the ancha and the sciatic vein was cured; and he magnified its effectiveness greatly. And he said that he did not need any other treatment, and that he was healed in one instance, until he recounted that perhaps he had entered a bath and exited it already healed.
And it is to be taken from green seitaragi; and if green is not found, let dry, fresh, be taken; and let it be ground much with some fat, and let it be placed over the ancha, where the pain is, or the leg, or the thigh; and let it be bound, and let it be left for the quantity of three hours, or for the quantity that the sick person feels a soothing of the burning. Then introduce him into a bath.
When therefore his body is made moist, introduce him into a bed. For the pain recedes, and it is healed.
And know that it is not fitting for anyone to use a cautery with these medicines, unless after evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides, who also said that goat dung, when cauterized with it a sciatic vein, is beneficial to it: and the cautery is made in this way. Let wool be taken, and soaked in old oil, and placed upon the deep place, which is between the toe and the heel, and is nearer to the heel.
Then take dry goat dung, and inflame it in fire, until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it upon the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished. Then repeat it. Therefore do not cease to do this, until the sensation reaches the middle of the sore, and the pain subsides.
And this method of cautery is called the Vaccinum cautery.
Concerning the cauterization of pain in the back.
Sometimes pain occurs in the back from many causes, either from an accident, or from a blow, or from an evacuation of superfluous matter, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and damp matter: and indeed cautery does not apply, except in this one kind, which occurs from the infusion of cold matter.
Therefore, after the patient's evacuation with foul pills, and similar things, let three lines be made on the back, where the pain is, according to the width of the area itself, after making marks with ink on each line with five cauteries, or more according to the amount that comes from the tolerance of the patient's strength: and let the cauterization be made with a cautery point.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries with a medial cautery blade, according to this form.
Concerning the method of cauterization in the beginning stages of a hunchback.
This illness often happens to young children.
And the sign of its beginning in children is: that a constriction occurs in their breathing upon lifting and movement; and you find in the last vertebra of the back and its joints that it has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
Therefore, when you see it and wish to treat it, then cauterize it with a cauterium that is circular according to this shape.
And let the cauterium take hold over the entire area of the vertebra equally; and if you wish to cauterize in a circle of the vertebra with a pointed cauterium, make two or three lines; and let the points be close together.
Then treat the area until it is healed with what we have said.
And beware, that you do not apply the cauterium to the hump which arises in spasm of the nerve.
On the method of cauterization in gout and joint pains.
When pains in the joints are from cold humors that flow to any part of the body, and when pains occur in the feet, it is customary for physicians to call that gout properly.
Therefore, when gout of a cold cause is treated with methods of cure, and the pains are not removed, then the cautery removes them.
And it is, that one should cauterize it after evacuation, in a circuit of the foot's joint, with many cauteries, and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
And if you need to puncture the surface of the foot, then do it with a pointed cautery. If the pains ascend to the knees, or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize it above each knee with three or four cauteries, on all sides, with this same claviform cautery.
If however more of this cautery is necessary for you, then cauterize it. And do not immerse your hand with the cautery, rather let it be about the thickness of the skin only.
If, however, the pains ascend to the knees and back, then administer what we have said concerning cauteries in its chapter.
If, however, the pains are only in the hands, then prick the points around the foci, as two lines revolve.
If, however, pain remains in the fingers, then prick them, over each knot, and over the palm of the hand.
If, however, the pains ascend after days to the elbows or to the shoulders, then cauterize both from every side.
And do not remove the sick person from a good regimen, from the taking of medicines. For if a good regimen is made, and phlegm is expelled, it will be healed with the help of God with this cautery.
Concerning the manner of cauterization in Ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the intestine, or the spermatic cord, descends to the testicle, and it is beginning to draw near: then it is necessary that you instruct the sick person to diminish his food intake in his daily diet. And let him use laxatives, so that the excrement may descend from his belly.
Then let him sit between your hands upon his back: and instruct him to hold his breath, until it emerges, or the spermatic cord, or the intestine, appears.
Then, reduce it with your fingers, and mark with ink beneath the rupture, above the pubic bone, with a sign whose extremity resembles half a circle towards the upper part of the body.
Then, cauterize with fire, of which this is the shape, until it turns white and throws off sparks. Then reduce the intestine, or the spermatic cord, to its cavity. Then let the attendant place his hand over the area so that the intestine does not come out: and you have now opened between the legs of the sick person, and placed a cushion beneath him, and another servant over his legs, and another over his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery upon that mark, your hand holding the cautery upright. And hold it until you meet the opening with it; or repeat with it another time, if you have not met the opening with it in the first attempt.
And carefully observe the exit of the intestine during your cauterization, lest you burn it, and death or great harm befall the sick person through it.
And know that when you do not meet the opening with the cautery, your operation is not successful.
And it is necessary that the cautery for infants be thin, according to their size.
Then treat with the remaining ointments until it is healed.
And let the sick person lie on their back for forty days, until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary that you provide sustenance for the duration of his treatment, which will soothe his stomach, so that the intestines do not exit during straining and defecation.
Then when he wishes to rise after forty days, then administer a properly made bandage, and let him keep it for another forty days.
And let him be reduced in labor, and in repletion of food and drink, and in loud voices.
For when he uses this regimen, he is thus healed with complete healing.
And I will speak of the treatment of Ruptures with incision in his chapter.
However, when ruptures occur in the rest of the belly, and are beginning, and the force is such that they should not be added to, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size: and let that which is burned be thus a third of it. Then treat him with what we have said, and it will not be added to.
And now some of the first have said that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this form.
After it is marked with ink, and a line is placed which is across the width at the upper side of the rupture, and another line at the lower. And place your hand in the middle with the cautery-iron.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Concerning the method of cauterization in pains from a fall or a blow.
Chapter XLVIII.
When, in certain limbs, pain occurs from a fall or blow, and that pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed cautery.
And let the cautery of every limb be a cautery according to its size, and its own smallness, and its weakness, and its own strength, and the location of the twisting, and the pain from it.
If therefore it is healed from the first cautery, it is well. If not, then repeat the cautery upon it.
Because it is customary for these pains to move from one limb to that which is near it. Therefore it is necessary to pursue them with cautery, until the sick person is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Leprosy.
Leprosy patients are sometimes greatly helped by cautery. And especially the type of leprosy that arises from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy: therefore, consider the power of cauterization itself.
If, therefore, the leprosy is unrelenting, and you have treated it with what we said in the division, and it neither recedes nor stands still; and you fear that the corruption may encompass his entire constitution; then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the known head, and a second below it towards the forehead at the end of the hair, and two above the two horns, and one behind above the nape of the neck.
And hold your hand with the cautery for a little while, until it imprints a small impression on the bone, and the bark comes away from it: so that the expulsion of thick vapors from it may be relieved, and cauterize the spleen itself with cautery, according to what preceded.
But if the leprosy has already spread over the patient, and appears clearly; then it is necessary to cauterize with these cauteries that we mentioned for the head, and with a cautery on the tip of the nose, and two cauteries on the two jaws, and two cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck, and six on the vertebrae of the back, and one large one on the buttocks near the tailbone, and one above it, on the very back of the buttocks; and two on the hips: that is, one on each hip, and two on the knees: one on each knee, and two on the shoulders, and two on the elbows, and two on the soft parts of his chest; and cauterize him on every joint, from the joints of his fingers of his hands and feet; and cauterize on every heel of his feet, and the joints of his hands.
And beware of the nerves that are above the heel, so that you do not burn them.
And sometimes a cautery is applied to the sternum, and another to the stomach, and another to the liver.
And know that the more you apply the cautery, the more help and benefit it provides.
And know that the sick person does not experience pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because his body is already numb.
And there should be cauteries of different sizes, large and small, according to the members and joints, in accordance with the variety of instruments that have gone before.
Then treat the cautery with flour of herbs and honey, and with other remedies, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a state of numbness.
When any limb is numb, and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not healed, then cauterize that numb limb with cauteries, according to the size of the limb, whether large or small.
And let your cautery enter the thickness of the skin a little. Then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And sometimes it is cauterized for some numbness that happens to the hand and foot, in the vertebrae of the back at the exit points of the nerves that move that limb, and the numbness is removed.
But let no one presume upon it unless he is knowledgeable about the anatomy of the limbs and the exit points of the nerves that move the body.
Chapter LI.
When Albaras is old and no medicinal remedies are of benefit, then cauterize above it with a deep cautery for a short time, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color is changed.
Then treat it with flour of herb, and lentils with rose oil, and arnogloss leaves, and pigeon's blood, and swallow's blood; of each, one part; mix these together, and spread them on a cloth, and apply to the site until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Cancer.
When Cancer is beginning, and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery around it, just as it revolves.
However, the wise said that it should be cauterized with the final cautery in the middle.
However, it does not seem right to me, because I fear it will ulcerate, and I have already seen that happen several times.
And it is more correct that it be cauterized around it with a circle, as we have said, or with many cauteries.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Adubelati.
When someone has Adubelati, and it is delayed in maturation, either because of excess causing it, or because of the patient's age, when they are feeble with little blood, or because of the time and need to hasten the maturation of the Adubelati, then cauterize around it with many small cauteries, puncturing. Then leave it. For it will hasten with maturation.
If however you want a perforation of it with a cautery, then heat the cautery, whose form is this.
And place it in the middle of the Adubelati, until it penetrates the skin: and let the cautery be from that which follows the patient, so that the course may be eased by purulent matter.
Then care for it until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a corroding evil.
Chapter LIII.
Corrosion is nothing but a corruption in a limb that wanders and corrodes it; just as fire consumes dry wood.
If therefore you see a corroding thing in a place that can tolerate cauterization with fire, then apply many cauteries with fire, small and large iron cauteries, according to what suits the place where the corrosion is.
Then cauterize it from every side until you eradicate the entire corruption, and nothing of it remains at all.
Then leave it for three days, and place on the cauterized areas ground sulfur with oil, until all the eschars and all corruption are eradicated.
Then treat it with ointments that generate flesh.
If therefore you see that after three days healthy flesh is born, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not: then again cauterize that which remains of the corrupted areas.
And it is sometimes treated with a sharp medicine by corroding. For it itself arises in place of the cautery.
However, cautery with fire is of quicker benefit; and I have already spoken of its cauterization with sharp medicine in division; therefore take it there when you need it.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in warts and corns.
Chapter LV.
This ailment frequently occurs in the lower parts of the feet, and it is a thick, filtered substance that harms the foot.
And cautery in them is indeed according to two methods: cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
As for cautery with fire, you should heat a concave cautery resembling a vulture's wing, made of iron, according to the size of the corn encompassing it on all sides, and with thin edges.
Then place it, heated, upon the corn. Then rotate the hand with the cautery around the corn, until the cautery reaches the depth of the corn, and leave it for three days, until it begins to discharge pus. Then plaster it with crushed wild herbs and salt, and leave the plaster upon it overnight. For it will be rooted out from its roots.
Then treat the place with a flesh-generating ointment until it is healed.
If they are not converted, and often occur on the surface of the body, especially on the hands and feet, then apply a cautery with hot water to them.
